Reader Correspondence

Three Policies for Saving the Nation

- Zhang Xiyu

To protect the fragmented land, to reunite scattered people, and to defend against the current national crisis, the government must first implement three policies:

1. Abolish the one-party rule policy, replacing it with a government of national talents. Integrate the Ning-Yue-Gui faction, the Northeast faction, the Northwest faction, and famous figures in and out of office, both civilian and military. Sacrifice previous personal rights and territorial thinking. Elect several people with great talent, broad-mindedness, fairness, and patriotism to take overall charge and build a sound government. Formulate a policy program. From top to bottom, all people should have the same goal, to discuss specific plans for resisting the enemy and saving the country, to know how to defend against the powerful, how to save the dying, how to gather the dispersed, how to reassure the people, how to eliminate bandits and communists, and how to consolidate security. Move after deliberation and enter after measurement. Those who can implement the national salvation policy should be supported by the people. Those who harbor ambitions and seek personal development should be driven out by the people. The government should lead in front and the people should support in the rear. All should be of one heart and one mind, and jointly face the national crisis. Order the strict dissolution of the current so-called provincial, municipal, and county party headquarters, cancel the use of national treasury for party headquarters expenses and the use of local public funds, to reduce waste and eliminate evil elements who use the party to exploit the people, so as to eliminate public grievances and eradicate the bad habits of warlord politics, and prevent their resurgence. In this way, the people of the world will know that the government is selfless and has the determination to change course with the people. It is time to issue a great call to rouse the public.

2. Organize a National Council for National Salvation. Set up provincial and county councils. Elect outstanding individuals from the whole country, the whole province, and the whole county to participate in politics, discuss all national salvation matters, and what should be promoted and reformed locally. Supervise governments at all levels, review budgets and final accounts. The government can be impeached and reorganized for dereliction of duty. Political affairs should be open to public opinion, and the many details should be held in the central government. Individual tyranny can be eliminated, and political integrity will come in time. If one party monopolizes political power, it has already misled the people into the pain of national subjugation. One faction fails, and the other faction takes its place. The so-called division of spoils may be repeated in the future. The melons of Huangtai cannot be picked again. The hearts of the people are not dead. It is appropriate for the youth, students, elders, and recluses of the whole country to run around, cry, and urge the government to rise up and save the country. However, the foolish government has no plans and only relies on the League of Nations for a chance to escape. If Jinzhou is lost, and the areas outside the Guan are ravaged, then North China will continue to fall. I fear that the situation of joint administration will soon appear and we will not even be able to relocate to the south and establish a small court.

3. Rectify the military. According to current statistics, there are about two million soldiers in our country, not to mention the bandit-style miscellaneous troops and local militias. Now, the government should issue an order to the military throughout the country to eliminate the old and weak and select the strong, with one soldier and one gun as the unit. The central government should organize a reorganization committee to assign them separately. According to the national defense situation and financial capacity, divide them into several divisions as national defense forces with definite combat power. They should be sent to the front lines in stages to respond to the national crisis. At the same time, a part of the military force should be used to suppress the bandits and communists. This is a temporary solution, but the fundamental plan is to implement conscription, which can eliminate the evils of recruitment, save national financial resources, and strengthen national power. This is related to internal affairs, and local autonomy must be realized, with household registration and specialized personnel. It cannot be done hastily. However, autonomy is the foundation of internal affairs, and conscription is the necessity of national defense. If those in power can choose the wise and appoint the able, they can do it quickly. Judging from the level of the people, autonomy should adopt a policy of intervention and conservation, not an extremely free policy, or a policy of slogans on walls. This is something that cannot be realized. Major military matters, such as warships, coastal defense fortresses, and improved armories, cannot be done without a long time and significant financial resources. If no preparations are made in peacetime, it is futile to discuss it in times of emergency. Therefore, I will not repeat myself. (Retribution)

Free Talk

Not Removing the Weeds in the Garden - Jifu Talks

Inverted Logic

Talks by Bu Tingzhai, weeding the garden, Cang

Chinese national affairs are topsy-turvy. This topsy-turviness is due to inverted logic.

Chiang Kai-shek said:

"Internal pacification must precede external resistance."

Sun Zhesheng said:

"Saving the party must precede saving the country."

My view is exactly the opposite of Chiang and Sun:

"External resistance must precede internal pacification;

Saving the country must precede saving the party."

Chiang and Sun may say that I have inverted the truth. I don't need to argue strongly. Let the facts prove it themselves.

Mourning Zhu Suoyu

- Zizai

Zhu Guwei Shiyu of Gui'an. A master of ci poetry. His calligraphy blended the styles of Yan and Liu. He was admired by the world. After the Qing Emperor abdicated in the Xinhai Revolution, he changed his name to Xiaozang. When writing poems or calligraphy, he used the aliases Qiangcun Oujun, etc., and did not use his original name, Zumou. He lived in Deyu Lane, East Youheng Road for a long time. He was close to his old friends Zeng Nongran, Wang Bingshan, Wang Xuecheng. They spent every evening composing poems and discussing art. After Nongran and Xuecheng passed away, he became lonely and unhappy. He often played mahjong to pass the time. In recent years, he was often unwell, but he still did not give up writing poetry and practicing calligraphy. A few months ago, for medical convenience, he moved to Guling Road. Dysentery occurred from time to time. Unexpectedly, it lingered for several months, and medicine was ineffective. On the 30th of last month, he passed away, leaving his friends and parting from this world. The people of China mourned him. I remember when he was the chief examiner of a certain subject in Guangdong, he had a minor feud with Cen Chunxuan, the Governor-General of Liangguang. When Zhu issued the exam questions, he satirized Cen a lot, such as "The inch of heart can be higher than Cen's building", "Spring is the word for foolish", "How can one get daylilies", etc. At that time, Cen was powerful in Guangdong, but there was nothing he could do about Zhu's rebelliousness. When I went to Guangdong last month, I met Wang Jingwu (Jingwei's brother) on Haoxian Street. He asked me about Zhu's recent situation with great concern and asked me to extend his regards. How could I know that on the day I returned to Shanghai, it was when Zhu returned to Daoshan. I failed to fulfill his trust. I feel very sorry. As I write this, I am filled with emotion.

Talking About Toys in the New Year of National Crisis

— Ms. Ye Hua

A garden without flowers cannot be called a garden. A home without children can hardly be called a home. Indeed, children are a comforting, sweet name full of all the hopes in the universe. In a precarious and weak country like ours, our expectations for children are all the more urgent. For the cruel enemy has left us with only one path of resistance: to settle accounts with the invaders. That is today's children. In our country's old customs, parents regarded children as either mere playthings or as servants. So-called love often ends up harming them. So-called education actually hinders their development. Such losses cannot be redeemed at any price. Therefore, this article is intended to advise parents to pay attention to the basic needs of children.

The basic needs of childhood are sleep, diet, and play. Sometimes they even play in their dreams. They eat while playing. Play almost dominates their entire lives. Play is a kind of natural and interesting activity. It can be divided into three categories: first, entertainment (Amusement), which is passive and aims to soothe the emotions and delight the mind with pictures and stories; second, games (Game), which involve dramatic imagination and have a specific purpose, such as chess and riddles; and third, sports (Sports), which mostly involve outdoor physical competition, such as swimming and boat racing. The use of toys is mostly in the categories of entertainment and games.

Toys are tools for children's play. They stimulate their imagination and facilitate activities in their imaginative world, imitating the behavior of adults. Although toys are small, they have a significant and profound relationship with individuals and the nation. For children are the future masters of the country. The suggestions conveyed by toys are deeply imprinted on children's nervous systems and cannot be erased. If these suggestions are healthy and lively, their educational value is immeasurable. But if they are base and vulgar, they will cause endless harm. At this New Year, as every household buys toys, I hope that people will not see them merely as objects for children to play with to amuse them. Know that they contain scientific elements and can develop children's senses of sight, hearing, smell, taste, touch, physical movement, and internal organs, and stimulate the growth of intelligence, morality, physical well-being, social skills, and aesthetic sense.

The selection of toys should focus on four standards: simplicity, durability, beauty, and affordability. Good toys have life and can stimulate children's own actions. Building blocks, beanbags, climbing ladders, balls, dolls, and animal models are toys that children will play with repeatedly without getting tired, and they can increase their creativity, self-confidence, and self-esteem. For example, bathing, dressing, feeding, and decorating dolls. Using building blocks to build houses, bridges, tables, towers, castles, and barracks. Sandboxes are often found in schools, but rarely in homes. I urge my fellow countrymen to set them up, so that children's natural abilities can be advanced. What they hear and see on a daily basis can be expressed through sandboxes. For example, the brutal acts of the Japanese invaders and their plans to save the country can all be seen in the sandbox. In the future, they will become pillars of the country.

The materials for toys should be rubber, wood, bamboo, celluloid, etc., so that they are easy to clean and durable. On the other hand, wool, mud, lead, iron, and thin paper are not only unhygienic but also not durable. The colors of toys should cater to children's psychology. The colors that children like are red, followed by blue, green, purple, yellow, white, and black. Younger children especially like light and colorful shades, which are inspiring and exciting. At a time when the nation is declining, it can inspire people to work hard and achieve something. Sometimes children abandon new cars worth thirty or forty gold coins to play with old square stools. Expensive stone lions, trains, etc., are not as attractive as broken watches and hats. A tree, a leaf, a pebble, or a bamboo pole in nature is better than any other toy. Therefore, toys do not have to be expensive, but they must be psychologically appropriate. They do not have to be bought from abroad; they can be made at home. Considering the ancient toys of our country, "hitting the earth" in the time of Yao and "kicking the ball" in the time of Xuanyuan are all worth promoting.

Age is inversely proportional to toys. The older they get, the less enthusiastic they are about playing. The period of greatest interest is at age six, after which it gradually decreases. By age eighteen, it has dropped sharply. This is a statistic from Cooswell's study of two thousand children. But we must know that babies can shake, push, and stroke toys when they are one month old, and can knock and ring bells at eight months. Toys that are easy to put in the mouth and are not easy to disinfect or wash should not be provided. Mouth flutes and harmonicas, which need to be blown with the mouth, should not be borrowed from each other to avoid spreading diseases. It is hoped that large-scale department stores will hire specialists who are familiar with the psychology of children's toys to guide manufacturers and customers, which would benefit the country and the nation in no small measure.

World Anecdotes

— Haike

Lip Makeup: Fashionable women in Chicago, USA, have a new trend in makeup. The color of their lips must match the color of their clothes. For example, if they are wearing a burgundy dress, then their lips must be dyed a dark red color.

British Female Mayors: There are currently thirteen cities in England that have women as mayors. Chief Justice Miss F. A. Farmer also serves as the mayor of Stoke-on-Trent. Her political reputation is outstanding.

Expensive Spider Webs: A film company in Los Angeles, USA, was producing a film. One scene required the lead actor to look out from a window covered with spider webs. However, it was impossible to create the spider webs on the window at short notice. Therefore, they had to send people out to find a suitable window. Eventually, they found one that was very suitable and offered a high price to the homeowner to buy it. They dismantled the window, along with the spider webs, and moved it to the filming location.

Glass-Topped Cars: A wealthy man in the United States loves airplanes and loves to watch them flying back and forth in the sky. Therefore, he recently commissioned a car with a glass roof so that he can look up at airplanes whenever he goes out in the car.

Records of the Officers and Soldiers Who Died in the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895 (Part II)

— Wang Yuanchang

Deng Shichang: Commander of the Zhiyuan cruiser. Held the rank of Admiral. Acknowledged as a Rear Admiral. In August of that year, he and Naval Admiral Ding Ruchang fought against the Japanese at Dadonggou off the mouth of the Yalu River. Our ships were repeatedly damaged. The Zhiyuan also ran out of ammunition and was damaged. Shichang was a Cantonese, known for his loyalty and courage. The navy was mostly composed of people from Fujian, who were jealous of him. They watched without helping. Shichang was furious and determined to fight to the death. He ordered the fast cruiser to ram the Japanese warship Yoshino. The Yoshino was the fiercest of the Japanese warships. It quickly dodged. The Zhiyuan was hit by a torpedo and its boiler exploded, and it sank. Shichang died, along with 250 others. None escaped. See my biography of Duke Duzhuang.

Chen Jinkui: Executive Officer of the Zhiyuan cruiser. Lieutenant Colonel. Died with Deng Shichang.

Lin Yongsheng: Commander of the Jingyuan cruiser. Promoted to Brigadier General. He joined forces with Chen and destroyed the Japanese warship Akagi, killing its captain. He was then hit by Japanese artillery, causing a fire. Yongsheng continued to command the artillery to attack the enemy, extinguishing the fire with water. Everything was in good order. Seeing a Japanese warship hesitating in the middle of the river, seemingly damaged, he pursued it. It hit a mine and sank. Yongsheng's skull was shattered and he died, along with 270 others.

Lin Lizhong: Commander of the Yangwei cruiser. Colonel. The Yangwei was damaged and ran aground. It was hit by the Jiyuan cruiser, which shattered its rudder blades and sank. Lizhong died with over 150 officers and soldiers.

Huang Jianxun: Commander of the Chaoyong cruiser. The Chaoyong was sunk by Japanese artillery. He died with it, along with over 150 others.

Xu Jingyan: Torpedo Officer of the Laiyuan cruiser. Right Wing Left Camp Garrison Commander. Originally named Liang. From Suzhou. Died in artillery fire. See Lin Shu's biography of Xu Jingyan. Luo Yong's Xu Xiyan Family Biography.

Li Zhi: Executive Officer of the Yongjing gunboat. Left Wing Right Camp Deputy Commander. From Jintan. The Yongjing was destroyed by artillery fire. Died in battle. See my account of Lieutenant Li. Two foreign officers, Ergelusi and Yu Xier, also died in this battle on the Dingyuan flagship.

Yongshan: Commander of the Horse Team of the Yiketanga Department of the General of Heilongjiang. In September, he resisted the Japanese at Fenghuangcheng and was ambushed and killed at Yimianshan.

Yang Shoushan: Commander of the Guangwu, Songwu, and Fushou armies. General of Zhang Gaoyuan. Died in battle on December 13 at Gaiping, as seen in the Jianshan Armor Notes.

Li Rendang: Also a general of Zhang Gaoyuan. Died with Yang Shoushan.

Li Shihong: Same as above.

Jia Junlian: Same as above.

Zhang Shibao: Same as above.

A Tale of Two Soldiers (3)

— Master of the Quest for Happiness Studio

Chapter One: A peerless courtesan lives alone, yearning for her beautiful companion, and a scholar fleeing his hometown forges a strange bond.

In addition, she had a delicate mind, a dashing style, a clear and bright radiance, clever and subtle speech, an outstanding spirit, and a healthy physique. All the different qualities that people desire in a beautiful woman, whether lively or chaste, heroic or gentle, can be found in her demeanor and deportment, satisfying the different tastes of those who admired her. Coincidentally, she was also at the perfect age of sixteen, transplanted from Suzhou to Beijing, and absorbed the clever and elegant qualities of both the north and the south, further helping her to rise to the top and become the pride of her youth, a perfect fairy. She firmly sat in the first place among the famous courtesans in Beijing's flower world, if not unprecedented, at least unparalleled. However, this wonderful person, through various coincidences of heaven, earth, and man, was produced with great difficulty, falling into the red-light district like Chang'e descending to earth. The wealthy and patrons who had the privilege of witnessing her glory realized that this blessing was not easily attained, so they were unwilling to miss the opportunity. Naturally, based on the principle of seizing the day, a wealthy and skilled merchant spent a great deal of effort and gritted his teeth to pay an extremely high price in the human flesh market, like an auction, to buy her. He hid her away like a rare treasure in his vault-like golden house. This man, who had particularly good luck and enjoyed the number one beauty, was said to be an old bureaucrat who had served as several ministers and later founded a bank. At that time, he did such a sensational thing, which truly envied many lechers and angered several patrons. However, he could not enjoy it for long. After only half a year of enjoyment, even his steel vault developed cracks for no reason and could not hold this living treasure. Originally, a fat and corrupt person did not have the good fortune or the ability to do such a thing. Relying solely on a pile of rotten paper-like banknotes to acquire such a fresh, lively, and peerless beauty was already excessive. Yet, he still acted against conscience, daydreaming, and based on some kind of ownership or exclusive right, insisted on treating the beauty as a plaything, imprisoning her in his house and selfishly enjoying her alone. How cruel and stingy was this! Could it be that the spirit of heaven and earth, which is very difficult to embody, and this rarest of beauties, were born solely to be enjoyed by such an old fool? No way! Regardless of face, heaven and earth cannot tolerate such injustice. He should wake up a bit!

Commercial News

Gold Standard Skyrockets

An increase of 15 taels and 4 maces. Yesterday, the gold standard rose sharply, the trend was very good, and it continued to rise. There was a slight fluctuation of 4 or 5 taels in between. The high and low for the whole day was only about 8 taels. Finally, it rose by 15 taels and a fraction. As soon as the market opened, it broke through the 700 taels mark. A large transaction suddenly saw a fall, and as foreign exchange, both official and unofficial, tightened, and the buying sentiment in the market was excited, the market price soared to 710 taels. However, major dealers such as Wu and others kept selling, causing it to fall slightly again. The after-market turned from weak to firm, and various firms came out to buy again. Statistical Table of Silver Dollars Deposited in Chinese and Foreign Banks for the 20th Year

When the silver market is loose, the amount of silver dollars stored in Chinese and foreign banks in this city is rarely noticed. This time, the inspection of warehouses has no major impact on the market. If the silver market is tight and the sources and uses of silver are active, detailed attention should be paid. After all, the current surplus or deficit in the Shanghai market has a significant impact on the market. At the end of the 20th year, when the silver market was transitioning from tight to loose, there were many people who needed silver dollars. However, the financial sector ignored this. The time when the annual bonus will be distributed is approaching, and the commercial market is depressed. There is no need to use silver dollars. Therefore, the bank's warehouse inspection report is not intended to be publicized to all sectors. Overall, the Chinese merchants' reserves are lower than before, and the foreign merchants' reserves are even lower. This shows that the current silver reserves in the Shanghai market are not abundant. In contrast, the total amount at the end of the 19th year of the Republic of China was almost one-third higher than the current amount, while foreign banks were more than two-thirds higher. Securities and Bond Prices Trend Upward

Trend is Peaceful and Atmosphere is Stable

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Exchange's bond market saw several spot trades opening, with continued activity in buying and selling. Futures trading remained limited to the January contract, with no transactions for the February contract. Bond fluctuations continued, with little change in the domestic and international situation. The bond market environment remained as dull as before, but market sentiment was more stable than before. The price trend was also much more moderate than before, without the significant ups and downs of the past. Statistics show that price fluctuations were mostly limited to around one yuan, with a general slight rebound compared to the previous day. Among them, the 1920 National Loan rose by one yuan and four jiao, while the 1920 Salt Revenue Loan and other futures contracts rose by eight or nine jiao each. The rest also rose by about half a yuan. Only the Consolidated 6% Customs Loan continued to fall slightly, while spot goods such as the Disbandment Loan and the 1920 Consolidated Tax Loan remained significantly lower than at the end of last year. The sudden rebound in prices is likely due to the significant declines of the previous day and the current low prices. There was some investment in the market, and buying activity slightly increased, which was a natural reaction after the decline. There were no other major reasons affecting the market. Although the bond market environment seems slightly more optimistic than before, the approaching Lunar New Year and the uncertain situation make it difficult to expand. It is feared that a strong rally will be difficult to achieve in the short term. The total spot trading volume for the day was 53,000 yuan, with futures trading reaching approximately 2.7 million yuan in the morning and over 1.5 million yuan in the afternoon, for a total of 4.23 million yuan.

Biao Fen (Standard Flour) Auction Suspended Yesterday Morning Due to Deficiency in Guarantee Money

Auction Resumed as Usual in the Afternoon... Limited Transactions

Yesterday's flour market saw the auction suspended in the morning before the opening due to guarantee money deficiencies, with the amount reportedly around 200,000 to 300,000. As the exchange placed great importance on this, the market was suspended. By the afternoon, most of the guarantee money had been collected, so the market resumed as usual. However, under these circumstances, there were few transactions between buyers and sellers. The initial market showed a slightly softer trend than the previous day. Later, as there were very few sellers, the market slightly stabilized. Looking at the future, as customer sales have been good recently, the market may temporarily stabilize. As a result, the price for the current month remained unchanged, February was down 0.25%, and March/April were unchanged, while May/June were up 0.5%.

Yesterday, the wheat market initially showed signs of stability, followed by flatness. Small Forum

A Small Declaration by This Publication

— Gou Fo

Stating the Aims of This Publication

Please Offer Guidance, Readers

The "Supplement to This City," originally an appendage to this newspaper, | the "Free Talk" everyone calls it the newspaper's "butt," and the "Supplement" naturally fits that category as well | but its relationship with readers, though different in terms of available time, is really no different.

The "Supplement" and this newspaper are absolutely different. The "Supplement" simply does not discuss politics or the overall situation. As the saying goes, "Here, we can only discuss the wind and the moon." The "Supplement" is originally a separate world, not standing in the same field as this newspaper. For example, in opera, the "Three Reports" sing grand, heavy-faced operas and old man operas, while the "Supplement" only performs small comedic plays like "Spinning Cotton" and "Fan Notes," etc. For example, in drinking, this newspaper is big fish, big meat, big chicken, big duck, while the "Supplement" is only a few small dishes of pickles and pickled cucumbers, eating porridge.

Since the "Supplement" is neither grand cuisine nor grand opera, the materials we select should naturally focus on the humorous, interesting, refreshing, and thought-provoking. Therefore, although the "Supplement" and this newspaper have the same relationship with readers, there is a serious/leisure distinction in the emotional impact of the "Supplement" and this newspaper on readers.

What about national affairs? So pessimistic and dismal. What about society? So chaotic and dark. Since we don't discuss national affairs, we should all think of ways to improve, correct, and guide social affairs. We don't want to be like "a blind man riding a blind horse, approaching a deep pool in the middle of the night," following the dark, degenerate society.

Therefore, the purpose of our editing the "Supplement" is to

Expose the superstition in superstitious aspects of society.

Expose the degeneration in degenerate aspects of society.

However, the so-called "exposure" of the "Supplement" is not to attack the privacy of individuals, but to attack common and general problems in society, or individual misconduct that can represent the general. We can only use abstract terms to describe them, and we cannot attack by name. This is the morality that the "Supplement" should uphold.

Shanghai is the source of culture in our country, and at the same time, Shanghai is also the den of all evils in our country. This is an undeniable fact. Promoting extravagance, promoting romance, promoting freehand style, and even adultery, looting, male banditry, and female prostitution are all special products of Shanghai society.

That being said, after all, the "Supplement to This City" is not a "Discussion on Shanghai Local Autonomy," nor is it a "Guide to Shanghai," attacking the corruption and darkness of Shanghai (or not just Shanghai) every day, exposing the weaknesses of Shanghai society in every article. What's the point?

Therefore, the second purpose of the "Supplement" is

From a negative perspective, it is absolutely not to cooperate with the dark and evil society, and we must issue a general attack order.

From a positive perspective, the "Supplement" absolutely supports and promotes literature, art, science, and so on.

For example, poetry, craftsmanship, painting, and all good deeds and special creations in society are all things that the "Supplement" is very willing to promote. However, the "Supplement's" method of promotion is not to seek from the large and distant, but only to seek from the small and near, not to seek a living from dry and tasteless places, but to seek a living from happy and interesting places.

Therefore, the tentative table of contents of this publication is

Small Forum

Popular Literature and Art

Popular Science

Street Sociology

East, West, South, North

Shanghai Stories

The table of contents listed above is only a hypothetical based on occasional remembrance. If we encounter better topics, or if we cannot be limited by the above titles, we will modify or add them at any time. They are not fixed and unchanging rules.

The reform of the "Supplement" is due to a hasty decision, so there was not enough preparation. Although we have this small wish, the editor's knowledge is limited, and we need everyone to help and guide us. As the saying goes, "A nun raising a pig, everyone serves it." This is the glory of the "Supplement" and also the merit of the readers. This is what all the "Supplement's" editors sincerely pray for.

Popular Literature and Art

Autumn Leaves

— Si

The wind rises,

Don't know how,

We gather into a pile.

The wind rises again,

Don't know how,

We scatter everywhere.

Who controls us?

Is it the wind?

We hate it—

We thank it.

We arrive beside you,

Or you arrive beside us,

If you don't pay attention, then don't pay attention;

If you trample on us, then trample on us;

If you pick us up to look at, then please do—

Everything is up to you.

Do we have some red color?

Will you take it as the charming beauty of spring flowers?

Or will you take it as the sad tears of blood?

Do we have some yellow color?

Will you take it as glory—

Or will you take it as withering?

We are still complete,

Will you think that our past is perfect?

We are already broken,

Will you think that our past is flawed?

We can't worry about so much,

Let you think what you will;

Maybe it is, maybe it isn't;

Maybe it's all, maybe it's none.

We are a pile accidentally gathered from all directions,

We will still go to all directions,

Taking advantage of the wind,

And form an affinity with you.

No matter what the result,

We all feel very happy.

Ah, the wind is rising again,

Please watch us, leaf after leaf, slowly drift,

If you wish.

Popular Science

Scientific Games

— Jing Shu

After finishing my lessons on Sunday, the wind and rain were gloomy. Several neighborhood children pestered me to tell them stories to relieve their boredom. I thought that instead of making up some magical and bizarre anecdotes, it would be better to take advantage of the situation and play some scientific games to instill common sense in them. The following are some of the things I searched my brains for, remembering what my teachers and friends told me (of course, I didn't invent them) and performed for the children, and they all shouted "Good!" I am writing them out to provide the children who read this publication with a way to pass the time.

(1) Flowers Appearing on White Paper Ask your mother for a handful of washing soda, dissolve it in clear water, and draw a bunch of orchids on white paper. Then take the vinegar used in the kitchen and draw a few flowers in the middle of the orchids. After the paper dries, it will be as white as before. Then ask a chemistry teacher for a little "litmus" solution. At this time, tell the children, "Look! I can spray immortal water to make flowers and plants appear on the white paper!" After saying this, secretly hold the "litmus" solution and a mouthful of clear water in your mouth. Chant incantations, shout "Diseases be gone!" and spray on the paper. Suddenly, blue orchids and red flowers will appear on the flawless white paper.

Reason After the children finish praising and laughing, naturally explain the principle to them, to avoid mistakenly believing in real magic. The principle of the above trick is very simple. Washing soda is one of the chemicals called "alkaline substances." Vinegar is one of the "acidic substances." "Litmus" is an "indicator" of alkalinity and acidity. It turns red when it encounters acid and blue when it encounters alkali. Therefore, spraying "litmus" on white paper coated with alkali and vinegar will reveal blue grass and red flowers.

(2) Fire Burning on Water Take a strip of rolled paper and secretly hide a small piece of "sodium" or "potassium" at the bottom end (sodium and potassium are both metallic elements and can be obtained from a chemistry teacher). Then fill a shallow plate with clear water. After the preparation is complete, tell the children, "I can make the paper roll burn on the water." Then lightly touch the water with the end containing potassium and sodium, and immediately lift it up. The paper roll will immediately explode and then burn.

Reason "Sodium" and "potassium" are both elements that easily combine with water, and they decompose water, releasing "light gas." "Light gas" is very easy to ignite spontaneously, and with the help of "oxygen" in the air, the great heat generated by the combination of "sodium" and "potassium" with water will burn the "light gas," affecting the paper roll.

Street Sociology

On the Public Bus

— Xing

Because of a small matter, I took a public bus to North Sichuan Road. This was exactly the day Jinzhou fell -.

Several men and women from the island country were already sitting on the bus. Each one had an uncontainable smile of victory on their face, and each smiling face was like a sharp knife, stabbing straight into my heart, making me feel a kind of indescribable shame and grief. I was silent, silently reciting the slogans of "Down with XX Imperialism" posted on the mirror frames of the shops on both sides. I thought, there will be a day...

Probably at the intersection of Bazilu, a woman from the island country, carrying two children, stood at the public bus stop, ready to get on the bus. I cannot determine whether it was intentional or unintentional, but the driver's compatriot did not brake and drove straight on.

Immediately, the men and women from the island country on the bus all stood up. Each smiling face was replaced with a kind of murderous aura, looking at the driver with fierce eyes, mumbling and grumbling in their mouths. Although I don't understand what they were saying, I knew they were questioning the driver for not braking.

Under the serious circumstances, the bus finally backed up. The woman and children from the island country got on the bus, and the men and women from the island country on the bus all stood up to give up their seats. A kind of passionate love for their nation was truly moving.

I fell into a corner, covering my face, afraid of seeing this group of cold faces. But I clearly heard that driver's compatriot muttering to himself, "Alas, this is the difference between people from XX country and Chinese people. If one of their women doesn't make it onto the bus, they all rise up to question it, but when our entire Northeast half of the country is lost, everyone is still calm, patient, and indifferent!"

East, West, South, North

Feng Yuxiang's Clever Response to K

On January 4th, Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, and Jiang Wenyu invited Feng Yuxiang to dinner at the Bankers' Association. Mr. Mu said, "Today, we have only prepared a bowl of soup, two dishes, and a plate of snacks, which is very meager. It is indeed unprecedented here. However, for Mr. Feng, who is frugal and self-disciplined, eating this is already unprecedented." After Feng delivered a speech on his political views, he also said that when he was in the mountains, he would drink two cups of clear water every morning, walk three thousand steps, and then eat four bowls of millet porridge with a dish of pickled vegetables, which he regarded as a daily routine. Then, he recited a couplet:

Two cups of clear water, three thousand steps,

A dish of pickled vegetables, four bowls of rice.

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (II)

Before Shanghai became a treaty port, it already had a city. During the Song Dynasty, the Shanghai Town Shipping Office was established. In the twenty-ninth year of Zhiyuan in the Yuan Dynasty (i.e., 1292 AD), it was changed to Shanghai County. The current Shanghai County seat is the original site of the county seat established in the Yuan Dynasty. This county seat is on the west bank of the Huangpu River, at 121 degrees 29 minutes east longitude and 31 degrees 41 minutes 15 seconds north latitude. The distance from the county seat to the confluence of the Huangpu River and the Yangtze River is twelve miles. The Suzhou River (i.e., the Wusong River) passes through the northeast of Shanghai County and joins the Huangpu River. Both of these rivers are transportation rivers connecting Shanghai with counties near Taihu Lake.

Shanghai is entirely situated on the alluvial delta formed by the silt of the Yangtze River. The surrounding villages have fertile land suitable for planting rice and cotton.

Shanghai has been a town for at least 2,154 years. Examining the meaning of the character "Hu" (滬), there is an explanation that "arranging bamboo in the sea is called Hu." "Hu" is a tool for catching fish. From this perspective, there is no doubt that Shanghai was originally a fishing market. However, as the coastline extended, Shanghai lost its original essence as a fishing market and developed into a large commercial port. However, Wusong Town, which is closer to the coast, replaced it and became a fishing market. Judging from this, Wusong Town will definitely not be a fishing market a thousand years from now. Perhaps it will become a more prosperous and important commercial port than Shanghai is now. The saying "seas change into mulberry fields, and the affairs of the world are ever-changing" is a perfect description of Shanghai.

Furthermore, examining the meaning of the two characters "Shanghai" (上海), they are the opposite of "Xia Hai" (下海, going to sea). In the early Yuan Dynasty, there must have been two bays extending into the coast. One of these bays was named "Shanghai" and the other was named "Xia Hai." Shanghai County in the early Yuan Dynasty was located in "Shanghai." As for where "Xia Hai" was located, it is not easy to investigate at the moment and requires further research in the future.

In the thirty-third year of Jiajing in the Ming Dynasty (1554 AD), pirates and Japanese raiders landed at that time, plundering Zhejiang and coastal areas. The Shanghai County seat was originally built with city walls to defend against pirates. In the third year of Xuantong, after the revolutionary army recovered Shanghai, the city walls were demolished and the moat was filled in. Therefore, people who come to Shanghai for the first time now do not know where the old city of Shanghai was located.
